si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If he inserts thorns into his eyes or into his throat or into his mouth or into the palate or shaves off his beard or cuts near his ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if he falls on his face, if he inserts or pricks and they are in motion;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the thorn in his right hand and place the cup between his two left-hand fingers, and gently hold the thorn against any one of these places until it comes out;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the thorn:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then find another piece of wood, or if you need to, cut it so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then extend it evenly from one side to the other, so that it can be moved, and hold the tooth in place with it, like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	If one part stops moving, then grease some oil on its two sides and push it in that direction, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if one doesn't move at all, then put this piece of wood higher up or lower down, and do so until it moves completely;
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back by constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must wrap him in a blanket, until he stops moving;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then place the cloth at the joint of the foot or the wrist, and in the other hand, do likewise to the other foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck at the birth, or it has a sharp head,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is necessary for you to pour the spiny sputum between your two hands, and move the head back and forth, and draw out the sharp liquid.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	Or take it with the instrument which is called an “almidah,” from which the form comes with the instruments or paste that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in this way I make it come out with a great natural movement;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then draw out the bones with nails,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the shoulder bone is forced out, so that it is split, as long as the moisture which is at the tip moves out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces so that you can move it.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or between the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is swollen on its sides, then the mild pull will move it, and the treatment of the mouth with mild treatments is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, then know that you should extract it with a towel wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and making the belly or the breast, as much as the moisture that is there;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other member is dislocated and the head stays put,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then take the hand of the patient perfectly by the palm, and pull it out to the mouth of the arm.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	and pour upon it .I. an ounce of wine, and make it fume;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth is tight from an abscess that has come up, so that it cannot be worked,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then provide wet and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and provide plasters, and cut in aqua molis et umida;
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if it is stuck on his ribcage, and you can put it back in place, then apply what we said about the live child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if we do not have the power, so that they are taken apart, and leave nothing of the second one.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, apply what we said about the feet that come in the mare (sea);
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if they come from the sea, so that it is dried out and restrained, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had one child dead, then another on top of it, and another that would die.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the twenty-one apothecaries in the pot, increased so much that it burst open and began to emit a great stench.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I stayed for a long time, but I couldn't hold back the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong poultice, and in it put a bone, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed, for this child's belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I wanted to heal the wound, and with great care, as long as the woman's condition did not improve;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and waited for a long time until she finally arrived, and there was a little bow at her place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter of the medicine only because that, when the master discovers a strange thing, he may know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to put back in place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here follows the form of pressing, where one sets the bones; and at the two turns to the two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be slightly thinner than the mandible, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let his mouth be two fingers wide, and the rim of the tree should be a finger wide, and long a palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and the three lines be two joints of this same stuff, which are joined together in one and in the other, a palm and a half long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joints are pushed into the mouth of the mandible to open when the two corners turn.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of the teeth;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and there are .iij. shoulders of the shoulder, if you see, of a palm long, and .iij. wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see open the mare with all the instrument, if so sit the woman on 1 bed, the legs during and the legs open,

puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand to all the instrument, if you have done it like claws evenly, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the mare, until the ball makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	All these instruments are all mounted, and multiplied for their appearances; and when you look at them, the operation is more quick and greater in quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument unless you have equipped it, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second one is retained for birth, command the patient to hold her hair back, and then cause her to sneeze, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose; and
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she sneezes because of it, that's good.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If he does not, if he can, and make a hole or lid, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the wound, as chamomile, fennel, anise, yarrow, camiline and centaurium.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, are boiled in water on the fire; then put a plug or lid into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the wound,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let the vapor come out of the wound; then make him cough, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If he does not, if he can, and make a hole or lid, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the wound, as chamomile, fennel, anise, yarrow, camiline and centaurium.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not heal, instruct the midwife to soak her left hand in oil of seed or in musk from the mountain, and then let it dry naturally.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and wants the second; and when she has found it, if she pinches it and extends it little by little correctly, so that the marriage does not crack at extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move lightly from side to side, and then draw; but it will come loose and fall out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marriage is tight, we have said the treatment of swallowing, and of steam from herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all those we have said, so that you do not follow at all in the treatment.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that he who is in the mouth of the mare, you tie him to the cunt of the woman, then the cauterize with ointment tetrafarmacon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	so that she who has put it in the mare, and then sets it on fire, and comes again; but nevertheless, when she puts it in, if it comes with a bad smell to the stomach and to the head, and bleeds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So that the smoke of certain things is useful for this; none of the ancient ones have tried smoking with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is such that when the woman is to be sterilized with smoke, this is how it should be used.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles a dog's head, and the thin end is placed in the nature, and the broad ends are on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the smoke be over the coals, and the hair be completely burned, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had the foundation pierced, but it is stopped with a subtle medicine.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So that the doctor who has the foundation pierced at his right hand may not pierce it with a needle and wound, and keep the wound from being infected.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a wet cloth of wine and oil, then the ointment cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that he will not recover, then put on a piece of leather and let his hands hang down, and be crushed when the child walks in bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And there is no need for sudden swelling of a wound or an abscess; if it is necessary to cover the sudden swelling: if you treat it as we said of the wine of plum.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodular and more painful than those that come from the fundament deflowered, or in the space between the iij parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, if it breaks open, and with a moist hot poultice or a subtle boil,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and never do these fistulas persist; and they are known by whom it is or excretion or wind when the patient has an excretion, and sometimes in a leap.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and if the fistulas perforate only to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they come up to the joint of the scrotum, and up to the tip of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	and so you know if the fistula perforates down to the perineum, and not down to the anus.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and so you should stick your little finger or perineum, and stick a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if he has tortuosity, if I but put a little string of horsehair, or .i. horse hair, as far as you feel the string or hair in your mouth;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no difficulty in passing wind or vomiting, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	be aware that it does not pierce; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persisting up to the bladder or up to the urinary tract, if in jumping the urine, and cannot be treated by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just up to the hip joint, then he must be taken by the hand up to his full length.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If it does not have any twists and the pain is continuous, then it is already bad, and it has not yet been treated by medicine or sudden remedy by feeling;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these persistent fistulas there is no cure but hard work, and the vain pursuits of foolish people who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not persistent and not old, there is hope for health by fire, as I have experienced,
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he leans down his legs until his knees, and has his knees bent toward his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of rain, or of mud if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	So that the patient feels the ground underneath, if it is convenient you put your two fingers there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then feel that the tent has been picked up; and if it is uncovered or you feel between your thumb and finger the syringe or the cane, then you know that it is effective;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if he does not work then he cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One should use the fire cautery to heal some people well, but this is not often done; however, it can be.

et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the doctor of the tent of water will saturate it, as long as that does not burn, and then the doctor of ointment will rub it while soaking and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this is healthy, it is good. But if not, otherwise it cannot be healthy;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if this is between the two and does not pierce up to the top which is at the base, and in front of the two there is a thick covering of wax or resin, and you see the fistula on that which lies under the covering of resin;

Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sun does not go out, and wind between you and the work, if the fire cautery or medicine astringent.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery gathers 2. things: that is to say, the burning of these dislocated joints, and the drawing out of blood and drying up of moisture.

puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then heal the wound with herbs that dry out the hard core, and are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is reset, then is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from the very foundation, and is separated from the body, it pulls at the root, and inquiries about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent, and enter. If it is the toe or the syphillus or char, where it is about to pierce, there is only one way of hope and faith, through the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not cut it too deep, so that you do not hurt the foundation, and let the excretion come out voluntarily through one side.

Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And no fistula is made in this way; and it is when you patch the tent onto the fistula, and she is or costs from the foundation of leather above, that
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if a tent is torn at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put .ij. of a tort in it, and bottle the tent to all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is persistant in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that torn, so that you bottle your two or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and train the head of the thread and assemble the .ij. shoulders together, and extract one from another, and leave it .i. day or .ij.;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it not at all, until the thread holds these shoulders that are between two, and they grind;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you can pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too completely enclosed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make the lacing cover completely, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spikelet from which one makes the fistula if it is sharp and pointed, part and trenches;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, for this reason one doesn't chop what one shouldn't chop, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids;
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	are in two ways: either they are deep within the fundament, as grains of resin, and small and large ones arise therefrom, and cut short there; or,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if one or more are there, and are far from the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are far away have little moisture, and
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and now again, where there is a little water of yellow color or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who have them in the foundation, so that you command the patient that he should sweat in bed, as long as the foundations are removed and the hair comes out.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it like a claw, or if you hold it with your nail, then cut it by its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot hold them because of their moisture, if they take them by the drapes, or by the cotton, or by a piece of cambric;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them with your two hands, then chop them up, and powder them on top of any hot powders that are in the place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as said above with fire cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then cauterize the patient with a sharp and biting cautery to wash out what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient is pregnant, and their cord is very tight at the fundus, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and are to be pressed with your fingernail or tweezers, and then are to be extracted, then are to be cured as we have said, until they are sound, and fear incisions made with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary to introduce the stitch according to this method: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, then bring the thread over and under the needle several times, and pierce the needle through from the other side, and tie the two ends of the thread together tightly.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is thick; and stretch the thread out, then tie it, and remove the needle, and do the same for all of them, and leave behind one [thread] to control the blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation .i. cloth dampened with oil or resin, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest until it has recovered, and when it is healed, if the wound is treated with ointment and other treatment, until it is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	do carefully at the end of its foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	For many times, the end of its foundation is dry in the intestines, and by nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you want to remove it at the root of a scalpel or your nail on top, which does not leave it wet;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat so long as he is soft, as it suits him.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot harden, then begin to shave more forcefully than before, until the hair grows out, and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat so long as he is sound
dou fremit	and then the fire will stop.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Fire is a small appearance of skin before the body, and it grows completely.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And no time does the wound hurt, and one can feel it like death throes, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an owl or a very strong vulture, and put that feather on the wound, until the purple circle covers the whole wound.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand over all the feather as much as you can cover the whole wound, and make it completely smooth, and wash the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then do this of a dog's skull or iron according to this form, and be careful not to cut into it and run over it.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut it, so that you keep the two together, and press them. And if you see, then cauterize the inflammation, as it is before or with the fire cautery of the chapter.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the blister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one should make blisters of silver or brass, or melted gold or lead; and no one should use these small or large instruments according to the purpose for which they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These children who are weak and suffering are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clister is small and large above, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a gap or the belly is tied, so that you see it, and the chest is pierced at one end, and open at the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or the ommet puts the medicines in a bladder of best or parchment, and pierces all around the little hole,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and place between each hole i.e. must of space, then pour in these holes a strong thread of twisted cord in 10 or 12, and join the belly together as if it were a sheep;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument lies before a strong thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And be the medicine not too hot or too cold, and oil or ointment of lamb's fat or some other thing, then pour it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then squeeze the ministers together with his two hands until it is completely full, then remove the cloth, and place the patient's legs against the wall,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he has medicine made, as much as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him with the disease of decay from the belly, and the medicine is hastening to come out, if he renews it as long as he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, so too is the cauterization as subtle as for a .i. child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the cauterization subtlety where the skin is held back:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the chapter on division; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are, and according to the places where they are made, and because of what causes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are from a stone, or an axe, or a knife, or a spear, or a club, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	ou that are done according to the rules of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the abdomen, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, beginning with simple head wounds, because the remedy will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is due to falling from a rock or similar things, and the skin is split but the flesh is not hurt, then you must first treat the wound with oil, and bandage it well.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you gently cut the aposteme: if it is a little wound on the head that has come from the sanc of the wound itself, and not the opposite way around, then you must carefully
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and have the patient abstain from wine and fattening meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If he does not eat, if his flesh is diminished, and does not drink wine or eat cheese, nor any other meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply to the wound, if there is an abscess, cotton dipped in oil and applied directly, or in wine that constricts;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, if the wound is fresh and not moved by the air, powder which I will speak about a little later on;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it burns, put on some ointments, until he is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be put together by tension, so they are put together by縫ing, like I say in the wounds of the belly, from the縫ing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	For if the wound is exposed to the bone, and it is open, and only held by a little, so the patch; then heal the wound with medication, and return it to hard leather in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large meats, like tests and wheat cake, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a boil that doesn't touch the bone, cut it all out, and then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein from which blood cannot be stopped by cutting it, then seek to find the artery, and if you find it dislocated, let it be as a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that doesn't help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then a light treatment is appropriate: and that you put this powder that hardens so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood seven parts; live chalk three parts, and the powder finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and the bandage form, until it is well dried and joins to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it not loosened, if it swells; for one should not wrap up the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make a paste of chalk alone; when you have neither incense nor dragon's blood, but the armpit has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if it has burned, it will have moved the wound, most certainly it is so, unless I put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or balls of flour made from water and honey until it is dry;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments as long as he is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if there is a fracture of the bones along with the wound, and it is small, then extract with careful pinches;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here after about the breaking of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the throat and it is simple, there is no difference between that and a wound on the head, but if the artery is cut at the throat.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the neck, if there is no other device to keep the wound open and prevent it from closing, for it will heal itself and close up. But if you put something in the way, it will delay healing and increase pain.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the circulation of the blood goes with the brain, which is the highest limb.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be made up, as if it were hot water washed in with oil of rose, and dipped also in warm water;
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones according to this method, and wetting with moist oils.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that it bleeds and needs binding, then heal as long as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she is full of bowels, so that it pierces or lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, so that she faints, and falls, and the fire cautery should be used in this case;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the windpipe is cut, or the throat, and the voice is lost, and the sound of the voice is changed, because the meat goes;
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	So that the taste does not touch on the tongue of the throat, and does not touch the throat but sets it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he comes back forward, and leaves it for a few days, then he cures with garlic until he is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then let him want;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, and if you can't hold them all together, and those that you cannot hold, let it be as long as the wound festers;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and strict with the dressing;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then heal it as I said in my chapter on the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	with a lance or a knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a cut from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look at the wound and see if the patient's breath smells bad: know that the wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not poured, and it is fresh to all of its blood, then I do not put the powder there at first hour, nor bind the blood so that it does not go on completely,
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and recover to the heart, and close up the wound;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put a healing ointment on it, and bind it 21 times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, then put wet cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient sleep on the wound .iij. days, or .iiij., or more often;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor bad trembling of the body or strange movements;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Cure it with remedies and other cures, as long as it is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, then operate so that there is a fistula; if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife blade and it is simple, or deep or on the back, then the cure of that which is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is great, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it has broken into the bone, and has made pieces, then examine the wound, and the deep wounds if they are unhealed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not unhealed, then let the wound heal, and then perform the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds to other limbs, it is the same judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	and for the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	is great and mild and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	causing a great wound, sometimes the intestines break, or the intestines tear, because of the impact of the bowels;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitch is more difficult, and there is no time worse than the little wound that the big one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for if you do not put the intestines back in place, step by step, if you do not put them back in place from warm to warm;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell up so much that they feel cold, if you do not put them back in place;
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for the little wound, for if you leave the intestine in its place more than others;
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The common two seams in the belly seam
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the seam of the other wounds of the body and .ii. other proper seams are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all of them are more proper with the belly seam, and I will say each one and I will declare:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestine out.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and a good thing is to put it back, this is done by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when he is fevered, heat him with some such method:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	moistening a sponge or .i. a napkin very well in warm water,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil water with squinant and cumin and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until it swells;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never done this with this vin, and is it not hot enough that you feel pain when you breathe.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestines with water or salt and cook them well,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this is the entrance closed to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small hole in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to make him sleep.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we do not cut him unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut into the core and leave it outside, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails are protruding,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is reset according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	If you can do this, for it is a difficult thing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	If you make the sick person walk on their two feet,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and keep his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part of the body called the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if he keeps his head and penis higher than the parts that are sore,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and if there is a rupture from the belly, it is in one of the .ij. parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you are aware that the navel part is higher than the other part;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to treat what I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, however, the equipment should be
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then put your hands .i. minister of mercy who seeth all the injury to his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	this is the common way of sewing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you squeeze a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	and leave from the top of the wound 1.2 inches, and stick a needle where it has 1.2 inches of good strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the 1.2 inches of skin with the 1.2 inches of thread.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	who is hidden inside the leather, as far as you make it go through from that side,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the 1.2 inches of thread together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the pulling out of a doubled thread goes through the needle from .ij. parts
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then put together the .ij. pieces of the wound in advance,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave 1 or 2 spaces, and then stick another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and never cease to do this according to what you need to do with needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	while all the wound is restricted;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are small, between thin and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the small needles fill all the space, and the too large ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this is convenient that they are moist.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and do not want to put the needles too far from the shoulder of the hide and the leather,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they do not want to cut and open the wound in front of the seam;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then close the head of the needle, so that it does not hurt the patient when sleeping;
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or tarps on the shoulder of the needle so that it stays in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it requires a needle or a pair of needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and you join the .ij. shoulders of leather and the .ij. shoulders of syrup together with one strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these shoulders all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you wind the thread around the needle in the manner in which we weave threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and set aside space between each seam the thickness of a small finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is seven inches long,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up an wound or abdomen,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was torn by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and this wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and there were also intestines of good length.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was on the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine; then it was eight hours old.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed just after .xv. days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miracle was that they said he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, because I was in .i. days where there is no ointment or medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put on a lot of honey on the wound every day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.;
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	And I will tell you the seven proper ways of sewing.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and dip it in the thread from the outside to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she has pierced the thread with the right thread from the right side, if you have dipped the needle in the dye or thread from the outside to the inside;
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and let her pierce it from the other side from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the meaning of this passage is that you should sew it as well as the skin-worker sews fur,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the suturing of one side, and take up that of the other, until the sewing is all done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of sewing, which Galiens describes properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is if if anyone does so, who assemble the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the heads to the other head, like this:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	file an awl or head of the needle nearest, and pierce that one only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the .ij. heads of the shoulder;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the awl, and pierce it from the outside part only up to that one inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	As the head of the shoulder...
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	And then pierce each and every part of the outside until you reach the center in 12 other shoulder chisels that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the method of sewing and it is the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen, then, thus speaks, and no one contradicts him,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	c’on doit coudre le ventre à .ij. aiguilles, ou il ait fils en chacune ;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew with knots;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is a stitch in the middle of the belly,
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds.
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the flesh has been moved.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you remove the intestine and the cut, then put powder on it, rubbing it in;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the flesh has been moved, then put any ointment that is present on it, as long as the wound boils;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the child, and let the milk flow, and the mirth.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it is well;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicine, put on it, soon that it begins to come out, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and stir it .ij. times a day until it is well.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicines in many cases when wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is appropriate for you to soak another light part in hot oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it between the arms, and release the joints;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it causes pain or swelling in the belly, and often happens.
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the black wine enema soothes, and rarely does the inflammation come up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it perforates within, and knows that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	the intestine called "jeun" cannot heal if it is torn,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the opening of veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and the approach to its nature of fire.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the arrow flies out of the wound, if he puts it back as well as the intestines, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it becomes yellow and brown, if you find the place that is black, that blood does not come from there;
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and take out who is between the thread,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two heads hanging from the side of the wound to the end so as to facilitate the extraction when the joints creak, and the wound is closed.
de la routure dou boueil	of the cut of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are runny, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If so, can he be restored to health in some homes?
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I see that a noble man was pierced or wounded by a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen.
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became a fistula and there was effusion and windiness;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will treat you as well as I can, and will not stop applying the treatment until you are well, and will bind up your wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that the wound was healing, I doubted that the patient had ill in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no evil, but delayed in good health, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said that when one has a small wound in the intestines, one should bind it in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take some tongs from a large testicle, then spread the lips of the wound apart.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the tongs have opened the mouth, place it on the 1/2 lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it pulls its mouth apart;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then place the cup on the head, and so it stays in place so it cannot release,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and so on. I. another will moan after in this way that before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and measure the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	For if it burns in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread that is moult dismembered,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread .i. a fine linen thread twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the needle, and sew the intestine, and turn it back in the cut;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of suturing wounds is not strong except according to the road of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, most especially when it is in one of the internal grooves, then there is no healing without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from fistula or whatever
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	says that any wound or abscess, once it has healed, is called a "fistula" universally.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most certainly when she is riding and running around.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And the fistula is according to the green doctrine hard and white, where there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also chewed like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and at times clearly in the clear sky, and at other times thickly in the thick sky.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	not at all times, and another time enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no pain,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is only by one of the eight-and-thirty causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by smallness of age or of wound;
ou por sa malice;	For his malady.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	For if he has a hard growth within him, and on the lips, so that it does not grow forth.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or if there is too much bowels.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or his loins are weakened, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine does not help in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where for fear that the corruption is a sign of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where in the area there is late digestion, and late health, and by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or organs:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have most thoroughly discussed all these causes, and signs, and remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient lons et igals; et s'il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu'il ne se muevent tant qu'il naissent.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For the spine of the back, or for any joint in the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if there is a pain that comes from the primary member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are great sanitation, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula so that it does not come to light until I have said so, and you are engaged in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you can see it clearly, then take a tent of rain or iron, that the fistula is straight if you seek it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then seek it with a subtle tent of water.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the plonk will bend within the tortuosity.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if it pricks his palm, you cannot well search for it with your fingers.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the blister is on one of the hands,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for if the moisture comes from one hole to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then search for it with your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and chop it completely,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well of the pain that he feels when you squeeze his hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in some of the places that I have told you, if the wound is along the line of the joint, or of a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and the bones are broken and the corroded chips that are within them;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until he is well.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if his fistula is very deep from the right place, it is necessary that you cut it perfectly, as well as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then dip them in medicinal water, and pour them up to the base of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excess that is reserved at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put oil on the sick horse as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	if it is not cured by this, then let him be cauterized as we have said;
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if his nose is corrupted by the fistula, then let him be mended;
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is injured in the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if his nose is open, and there is corruption and blackness, let him wait until the whole bone is corrupted.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal him of things that cause trouble as long as he remains healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not healed, and his bowels are upset as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	So that you are not troubled any more than necessary:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	If you see it, and wait as long as you can.

Des vils	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more is taken away from the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must not administer any kind of purging at all, and then treat the disease from the base.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure for iron is done according to three ways: one is by copping and drawing out the black blood; another is by
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is if you feel the vein, and then treat it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size is determined according to this method: raise the first leg of fresh water, hot, until the thick skin is slightly stretched.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then stretch the leg of the sick person from the hip all the way down to the knee;

et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then let it lie, and he commands that he be dyed with black dye;

Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The alleviation of the pain of the patient is done according to this method: raise the leg of the patient, if there is hair,

et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, warm it by the fire, and then hold the long side at the hip joint, or in the lower part of the thigh to the ankle.
