puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then trawl and peel it up to the second size; then remove it by size until it is all gone, then cut it;

et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not tear, for if it tears, so you cannot pull and lift it up, and it causes harm to the patient;

De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and land that does not have moisture.

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between skin and hide
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "beef disease" because it often afflicts cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and hide, and goes everywhere up and down the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it smells good to the member's alarm as it goes from one member to another, until it turns the hide where it went, and jumps.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with certain humours, as they come towards and wind around, and shine, and worm-like creatures or eggs in the belly.

par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	then enters and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, so can one only go:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	If it is then necessary that you keep the place dry by a strong knot well tightly tied,

et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is appropriate to use the patient of purification of skin with soluble medicines for the bad humors that are produced,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if he is cured of meat that causes putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	For pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vacir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it spreads from one limb to another; and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered some of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then I saw it rise like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	as soon as possible, like a sharp silver blade when it cuts from one place to another;

et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it runs through the whole body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then he told me that she twisted her body, as I saw it;
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how she moved her member from one to another, for I have never wanted this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had heard that many people who suffer from this disease want to move their pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have never wanted it, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that perhaps because women have narrow waists and open veins;
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this it seems that the wind has been forced out by constriction;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicious, and have moist hearts and relapsed veins.

Des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the type of feather used for them.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have .ij. angles, and those that have tongues, and those where there are pieces;

si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members;
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls to the ground then you shall know that she is dead, I will tell you what below.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is convenient for you to extract this arrow, for death comes after many preparations;

est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when amputation, sweating, and twitching in the limbs, inflammation and swelling of the tongue, spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of phlegm;

et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign reveals itself, if you keep the cure, and treat the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is shot or struck, is that it is near to the left breast, and also as if it were lodged in some hard thing, not in a void place.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like a bird, and in dark short breath, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and faints.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you will have no doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that is shot out of its sheath is that there is no foam in the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he/she gasps and feels cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters the shell of the shoulder, then it tears the small ribs; and it gives great pain and a great sighing; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters the stomach, perhaps some meat will be wasted from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters the belly, and through the intestine it does not come out, there is no hope for recovery, neither for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters the bladder, and with it the urine jumps out and goes away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and leg and foot, and similar limbs, are safe according to many provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the neck or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you that it has happened to me, do not make any other way.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There came to one man an arrow where it entered in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled it from the other side through the grease of the ear, and was cured without feeling any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And tie an arrow so it hits deep in the fat of the oil, taking off the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was removed, and I could only see its tip toward the furrow.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large of an arch-blue, all .i. heavy without ears; the game was clean, and there came no bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And tie an arrow to the neck of a Christian, and the arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loved the beard, and I made it grow longer than before, and the Christians were healthy.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And tried an arrow on a man, that it struck his leg or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after three days, if not his condition changed;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow, engaged it, and shot it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to go to a man who has an arrow in his chest or back, and the wound is sewed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and do not change its natural position within, and
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	do not find fault in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow has been shot into his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it endures much pain to suffer; and more like these.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And take an arrow from the king of the knights, that he was missing his eye, no need for an arrow shot.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was a little nghiêng to the right side; and the arrow was all re-set

Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried all of my efforts on her, and I did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and trouble in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the point of an arrow

et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I showed him how to extract the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the plaster on every day, and resolved the wound very quickly, and delayed it for a long time so that the patient would not be in pain.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	for as long as he felt the arrow; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive aqueous medicine every day, until it was open.

et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and I crossed well the boundaries of three months,

adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I ceased not to study and devise methods of instruments, until I had taken it i.e., a day
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to that which its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I have held it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirage judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I held it and then sewed the wound shut, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or t’ai said the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you place your treatment on those whom I do not mention, for the book cannot take them all into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the master sage chooses only a few small things, and for those who are present and failing;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	truly nine operations, and nine instruments, in the dismemberment of strange things that come into this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows should not come from the limbs except according to these 17 ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out of its normal place, is an arrow entering into its flesh, and does not jump out at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, let her leave the car while it is rotted in, and let its issue be heard.

et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and so it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, then it pierces all the way through, as long as the hole inside is enlarged, and then the injury is done.

car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if an arrow comes to the body just a little, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if an arrow is not stuck into the bone only, and comes just a little,

Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is very stuck inside and cannot come out, then give it a massage, as I told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the heart, if one cannot see it, then search for it with all your might.

Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where it does not open anything of him, or the skin is swollen in a certain place if one sees it or feels it apparently:

Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the form:

Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	and the remedy for these three diseases is with the use of heat, and with pressure from a mallet, and many illnesses, and with vermiculin, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and scrofula;

et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master stands over the head of the patient, and the patient cuts with a scythe on one side;
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein well long little widely, then treat the pain temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then make another in the other vein, then massage the leg, and extract the veins gently,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	to prevent the patient from choking; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The patient must not eat or drink anything until the wound in the lips has healed; and he must be careful to prevent any damage to the gums, cracks in the lips, and the birth of teeth, and swelling inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this treatment is that the patient should sit in front of you, and his neck should be held in place as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip over, and look at the two openings, one on the right and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by what color they are, and by what color they surround the small openings.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So then they both come together, and if you do not know them and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So then take the biggest of the two parts, and do the same for the five veins that are above and below, because this is a similar method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the side of the neck
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	From the side of the neck:
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the medicine is that the patient dies between your hands before the sun, and the liver turns black, and looks down at each side with a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Heal therefore both of them, and do not become too perfect in doing so, for the arteries are within.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the back that are commonly healed are healed according to .ij. manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where one pierces with fire a wide flame, and with a sharp knife the olive-leaf, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the largeness and the narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is thin when it is named moist, and is wide when you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is a task to open the flat veins that appear with thick blood, which contain thick blood and trouble;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle than pointed, and is for saving subtle veins, where there is subtle citron-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cure for the bazillar vein, which is one of these veins, is good for diseases that affect the throat, neck, chest, and stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the healer should cauterize and bind the artery that is beyond it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he stops the artery, and the blood flow stops, then he should bind it tightly, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be held by fire but be cut off like a horse's mane.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	If the nose does not open clearly, then you must extract it and change it with another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you do not see any blood, or if you feel the vein pulse in the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and hold it to the fire as we have described.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know where the vein is, it is also necessary that you extract the arm, and touch the spot until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot for the incision, then tie the arm, and cut the vein from the flame in secret;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the spot bleeding, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see urine rising high as a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten yourself, then, and set your shoulder to a long time, and then loosen your shoulder without straining, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the arm rest and leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move it until it is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not dislocated, and you will come to me, and the medicine is not given to you, then open the artery, for the head of the shoulder is dislocated; and hold it steady.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig tree, and make it, and take one of the halves and set it well up until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it does not bleed, it is good; if not, if the healer, as we said, of the powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the blood is not due to multiple conditions for the small size of the wound and the possibility of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of the vein in the middle is treated with fire so that it stops flowing from the top of the head and the neck.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	For this reason it is composed of the basilical and cephalic veins, as we said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is fitting for the physician that he be careful of the nerve which has been stretched, and if he cuts too deeply and completely, the nerve will be torn.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the patient swells and his health is damaged, and perhaps cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any way because of its lightness, then you must heal the instrument carefully; avoid damaging the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then divide it longwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cure for the headache of the shoulders, so it hurts the neck, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to heal with fire from the olive tree or from the mirrin tree, for this is the most salutary of all veins, for it does not affect the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one should always start with the lighter treatment first, and do no harm the first time, and then start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And in case one hurts some men the first time, it is no harm done, but it is no harm if one starts again;
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about a healer, is that healing should only be undertaken to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses from developing.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	The healer should be skilled in one of the three main areas of healthcare at the time: head, face, or gut.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it is necessary to take care in the beginning of pregnancy, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it is necessary to take care the first day or third day, after 1.2 hours or 1.3 days every day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The remedy that is administered to the sick person does not have a fixed time, but rather it should be taken at specific times and intervals;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to take care of children before the age of 12, and women only after four months until seven years;
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They are not to take the old men who have lived for sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone is saved, in any way, it is necessary that he dislodge the intestines of a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained mucous from the end of the nose, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous mucus that is harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not save those who are too sore from meat, or who are greedy, as long as it is possible, or droopy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and he will be affected by the pain after colic, and vomiting, and stomach upset, and frequent sexual intercourse with women, and childbirth, and staying up late, and anything that depletes his vital force, or by something from his weapon or heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then carefully the humors, he becomes thin first, through meat and beverages and medicine if you have used it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter or bathe, if nothing harms him, carefully to reduce his fever;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein with a third part of the blood, as we have said before;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard him from work and from fasting and from lust and from similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be quiet and still, and let the doctor who is higher up than you heal you, and rub your arms. 10 times or 12 times,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then pull the ligament slowly, for when it is too tight or short, it cannot be cured;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub it with your hands until the veins swell, and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the skin with a little old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein at the place where he wants to cut,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not run and it is not hurt by iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings when cut, and some that are easily winded,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts on the fire, if one removes it, the vein cannot be opened, and thus is one of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens a vein, if the wound is too narrow, for in these things it is necessary that the doctor be warned.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if he opens the vein for the first time, that is good; but if not, then let him begin again a little bit lower or on the back, where the legs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if his legs are swollen and the patient is hopeful, let him rest for a day or two, and do not tie his arms.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for in case he comes to an abscess; do not go into the bath, and then begin again the cure if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the rib is broken, or the lung is pierced slightly with care and doubt that it does not hurt as much as you see, then be confident in this broken rib for all the fire correctly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little healing, so that the veins are swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swollen, do not put salt on it, and put a little oil on it, for it cools the body's heat, and is soft in this vein due to the oil that it has;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each wound that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this middle makes the triangle and bow of ears, when one lays it on its place; so subtle is the sinew and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess that is big, which happens many times, most of all when it is not inflamed except at that time or when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and put on top wet sponge in water and in silk a little warm, and holds it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the exit of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days no black or green color, then it will not hurt;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on none of aloe or myrrh poultice in juice of mint, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of the disease in the bazoo: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch when pressed with your hand, then this is the appearance of the evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So don't put on any of what we have said, because perhaps in the court without the artery; but make him a dry plaster to harden the place, then heal it with other remedies, until he is well.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each pain according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is without heat, let it be until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it be until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it concerns the one who is flat and dry, and has a need for blood extraction, that he make a wide wound, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and you must heal it often, and you must heal it by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of healing is saved from the corruption of blood and the stretching of nerves, and it is better than long-term healing;
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose pulse is in sickness, it is appropriate to give moist bread in grape juice; if it is heated up, then it should be eaten three or four times a day.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complex, if he drinks before the sickness moist bread in syrup of musc or in honey syrup aromatized with spices, if as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it has sweated at the sickness's exit, after drinking water from blood, it is appropriate that he sniffs brot of beer and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use of the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his arms and sometimes other things, when it is necessary, as he weakens with great sickness, so that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits up his arms after the first healing, and he has a strong corse, so that he heals .vij. hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who should be healed from another part, should be healed two days in a row.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has internal heat that warms the body, and brings fever; if so much is drawn out, and the opening widened to the extent of a pea, then:
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and then that you treat all types of disease, and place your hand on his pulse when he heals, so that death does not come in the place of a priest.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and if it happens again, when the healing has been neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not come until you see the shoulder separate again, and close it, that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, extend his arm carefully, for this would be wrong;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be so that it heals the second time; or you i point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood which is frozen in the vein comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .i. piece of string soaked in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it be so that he does not compress it, as long as the abscess is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, draw the blood a second time, so that it heals in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is cut at its base because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of the cut is so that the patient dips his hand in warm water until the feverishness is gone.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then he should move his hand gently so that the vein appears clearly, then cut it now, not wide nor long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And make the incisions wide and cut well next to the joint of the hand, and don't be able to pull it out, then dip the hand in warm water, and leave the blood running in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is not yet healed, then do not re-break my hand in warm water, for we treat it more in the cold than in the heat;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the wound of this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	the salve for the right hand's wounds is worth all liver diseases, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	remove the hand, and dip it in warm water, until the vein is hidden, if we see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the spine is bent, and you chop it from top to bottom, it does not hurt anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not cut too much at once, for the nerves are all exposed.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then dip the hand in warm water, so it freezes into the wound and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as much as necessary, put oil and sutures on the vein to hold it firmly in place, and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The medicine man must treat the disease of the mouse with his left hand, and do all that I have told you to do with the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The medicine man must treat all diseases that are located in the chest.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	To treat diseases of the heart and hold back flowering, to cure diseases of the legs and knees, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his medicine is that the disease drinks small amounts of hot water, and rubs the vein until it dies.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and put it above the ankle joint; and if the vein is at the foot, then go over the foot with more rain.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And make it as wide or longer as necessary, or at the ankle, so that it does not hurt.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, do not worry about the nerves that may be affected, and heal it as you would a wound, and let the fire go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get out of it, put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to cauterize for the first time, then begin again on top of that a little bit, because the leech is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerve, if it is as we have said, and in this way do the same with the other stone evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leech of the vein is to be put on the heel, and its sourness is worth the pain of the knee, when it is for bloodletting.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its sourness is that the patient goes in or out of the bath, and strips off from the heel.iii. three things in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so that the blood flows in all ways that you can, and crossing over.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and wait until you cut it, for its line is out, and it is much renewed by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not cut it, so that the rain of the line opens or closes from the foot, and towards the small day, and guard against the danger.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make so much blood flow that you see it, and then wash the line, and put it on cotton and hold it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuums of suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made from horns, or of air, or of glass; and the suction is done in 13 ways: either by piercing and drawing out blood, or not piercing but drawing out by a kind of force.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction that is not done by piercing is done in 13 ways: either it is with a sharp instrument or without a sharp instrument.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and suction that is made by piercing and drawing out blood is done in the following ways:
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	for the head is one piece with the neck; and the others are joined to the collar.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and there are two in the collar, and one at the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and one at the shoulders, and one on the back of the neck, and one between the eyes.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ones that cover the arms, and the ones that cover the legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction of the .ij. feet; and the suction does not treat blood, save that of small veins that are scattered in the carriage
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and so you do not affright any, unless it is a small vein that is spread out in the carriage;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be mixed with anything, nor burned nor chilled, in any disease that comes from overindulgence, until the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity it is needed to suction, or through custom, let us make it uniform every hour in the beginning of the month, and at the end, and every ten days;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are many who, when they have the need to ventilate, become very heavy-headed.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if it is true that people who are venting and have a flush on their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who are venting a drop of blood in their mouth, and have escaped the tongue, and feel thirst for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see vision, and death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and most especially when it is damp in the month of May, we order them to be breathed on after iij hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The treatment of the disease of the head with the help of the herb called marjoram ... which comes out, and does not come until all the body has been evacuated;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this breathing should be in the place of the treatment of the head;
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not come until those who are of a cold complexion and have a headache, because this makes them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason I am not sure it is right to use it while sleeping or those who have a cold or feverish illness.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are healing from it often become confused, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little further down due to the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction at the neck is in place for healing from the throat and base of the nose, and for this reason it is also used for cutting into the stone.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut through the channel of the pancreas, and all around, and to refill.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push back, for if it holds too firmly, there is danger of injury or stomach or bowels.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventresses are the winds that come from the colo with pain in the head, and blindness and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the saint's basil; and it is necessary that you instruct the saint to express his hand for a cut, so that he does not chop the artery, and do not cause an escape of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventresses bring about the death of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the saints' lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are a disease that comes from heat and filling up.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The windings of the arms also cause as much pain as three veins in the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And commands the patient not to cut too deeply, for the bones are bare and the arteries can be easily cut.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the back so it reaches the foundation of the disease, and the disease of sore breasts, it is necessary that the ventouse be large and of air, for her work is to milk well; and if by chance it was thin, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg ventouses open widely, for they draw blood from all the body, and they are good for old pains of the joints, and of the foot, and of the bladder, and they remove the flowers; and they are in the place of the iij. sophens, and of the iij. ankles, but they weaken the body after a long time, and bring death in many situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the ventouse is that you put it first, and suck quickly, and put it firmly, and stir evenly, and do not cease to do so, until you see the red and inflamed place, and the pain of the sanc; then stop, and remove the ventouses, and take care of the condition of the bodies, for there are some who have bitter heart: so it is necessary to stab once only, and to make deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the sun is thick, it is necessary to stab twice: the first time to soften the path of the thick sanc.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if he is very thin, then it is necessary to hurt him for the third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we must press hard only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to draw blood repeatedly, then we should do so often; and if he is thin, then we must press hard completely, and the end should be that the pulse be felt abruptly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover those who have thick and tough skin, and who are rough, so that you rub the areas with oil that opens and dissolves:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or squash seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in an ivory case, of oil of mustard, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the excess is thick and cold, then take oil of amber, or of balsam, or oil of fennel, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	and if the one who suffers from acute heat and wide pores, then it is not necessary to put oil on,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the exposure to warm water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have moisture from the mouth, if they rise thus, or from water of mirth, and from sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses rise up from old wine, or from water of oak, or from a infusion of fennel or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and they should not go out into the sun before a bath or take a bath, but an hour or two after; and they should not sleep after wind-sucking.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be washed, when he needs to be wind-sucked, and when he has been wind-sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are coleric, and whose temper is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it happens that he applies cold things, as pomegranates and endive and lettuce to the skin, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and soaking in puddings, and char of chastity, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion, if they apply syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and soaking in puddings, and char of chastity, and moist meats.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and as soon as he begins to breathe heavily, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people three times or more aniseed or mint before or after wind, to support the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle with the water, but it is necessary only for those who are warm.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The fists that are placed to hurt are those that are placed on the liver, and the mids, and the Podagre, and on the belly and the buttocks and the reins and the vagina, because this member does not suffer to be hurt on the outside.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and do not do so except to draw blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the teats when the newborn is healthy; to remove the viscous substance that is in the limb, as we put vipers on the belly and on the breast to reduce the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an operation or a stone, if by its attractive virtue it may happen that the operation takes place, or it removes the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus does it act when put on the liver and on the gallbladder when there is repressed wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are empty, but never together, and never water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as well as the disease of pleurisy, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water or with water in which herbs suitable for that have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	and has .ij. inches in length and half a palm in diameter, and is placed so that the middle of it is about .i. inch from the edge, as for piercing with an needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and of rain, soufflé before so that it does not burn the patient when putting on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a stick of wood or iron, to put a candlestick grip,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they shall be large and small according to the illness and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the plasters for children are other than for old people, and thin ones are other than for fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one put this suction cup onto the limb?
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the wax candle or ointment, and place it onto the ventose over the penis that is placed onto the ventose,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the ventose so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it onto the limb, and these two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when one sucks, if there is steam, and one puts the ventose;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the poultice often, as you have learned.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	For the wind-pump which has been opened up because of pleurisy, there is no need for a wick or piercing, and it should be placed lightly on the limb only when it is dry;
et c’est li forme:	and this is how it is done:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	For the small members such as lips and teeth, and similar things, where wind-pumps cannot be placed due to their size;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and strip the lees from the wine, as two or three new wineskins, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is that when you find them that are in fresh clear waters without danger, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in water in fresh clear water until they are familiar, and do not have anything in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then soak in water from the vein and from the tub, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the lees;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and cheerful, if there is a place where it can be put a suction cup, put it there, because that's worth much more.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the joint then, and then with water, very well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the head is too warm after raising the joint, then soak it in cold water, and put a linen cloth on it, and keep it there as long as the blood is stopped;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is multiplied, then put on vitriol powder, or garlic, and similar things, until it is stopped;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Here is the translation of the first line of the text:
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work to do, so take others without saucing."
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the sausages don't want to take it, so rub the fire on the meat, or you put an needle in it until the sausage comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and soon as they feel the fire, they heat up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, if you powder a little aloe and sawdust, or ash, if they cry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is how the book of fractures begins:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	For in the art of medicine, this chapter is necessary, and it is a cure for broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the wise man will pour this chapter of the book upon him, which he has never seen in any of the ancient books, nor has he read a letter about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason the science is strange to us in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing about it, except from the science of ancient books, where I studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the preceding two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sum of words and the chapters where wisdom is found, and delay on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing totalls him, so as weakness of the corsage, or enfacement, or age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break, or dislocation, or torsion, or breakage to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing totalls him, so as weakness of corsage, or enfacement, or age; or if his temperature is very low, or too often feverish; and eat cold meats often, this is to say, cold joues, and char of onion and garlic, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fat foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot apoplexy, or an increase of matter in the limb; if the sick person returns to his first state of health.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken nose begins to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the sick person with meat that produces great fatness, or viscousness, such as cooked bread and rice and beans and peas and pork and venison and fish and strong wine and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a slow healing of the break begins later and more slowly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot well heal or harden according to their nature because of the loss of members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But it does not heal, set the broken bone back in place - that is, the thick ribs which join the member together, as it was before; and do not at all take away from its work, and because of this it is necessary to increase the flesh, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are different kinds of broken bones in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break in the head is different from the break in the leg, or the foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes around the ear, and another one with the thistle, as if it were the size of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if a break with a wound, and a break all over a little slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each way there is its own tool, and its own implement in the restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known the break of the bone by what its turn is twisted, and wide apart well by the other, and some at the presser of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting of the neck, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have a twist, or a break, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it by hand alone, but put medicine on it which comes later, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which comes in the arm, and are the two parts separated, it is now necessary to make them equal, as well as the bones of the foot come;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if there is a hard swelling, let him not leave it any longer than until the swelling has softened.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then cut it evenly at the top so that you can move it easily and cleanly, and know that the healing of this is easier than the healing of that which has pieces; then hold it in place, as it is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there is a broken bone with pieces, and it is healed from one-half to two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or at the hand, if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb back in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the member have healed, you do not add anything to them at their place, as it is appropriate for you to make a fire cautery on them, and keep from your work so that there is no injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well set together the .ij. shoulders of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well by the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if it is held firmly, and does not strain too much, do not press it as they do who make an incision in an abscess, hot and contracted in the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in order, if you teach the patient that he not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, unless it is a little, and the necessary thing is to put him in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure he is straightened correctly so that twisted movement does not come about when he is healed;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
